                <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt; TEXT-ALIGN: right" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: times new roman">&#160;$&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;

      &#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;-</font></div>

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The

      <div id="FTR">

        <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">7</font></div>
        <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">

      <div id="HDR">
        <div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;

      </div>
    </div><br>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;NOTES
TO FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">June
30, 2009</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">NOTE
1&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;ORGANIZATION
AND NATURE OF BUSINESS</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Northern
Oil and Gas, Inc. (the &#8220;Company,&#8221; &#8220;we,&#8221; &#8220;us,&#8221; &#8220;our&#8221; and words of similar import)
is a growth-oriented independent energy company engaged in the acquisition,
exploration, exploitation and development of oil and natural gas
properties.&#160;&#160;Prior to March 20, 2007, our name was &#8220;Kentex Petroleum,
Inc.&#8221;&#160;&#160;The Company took its present form on March 20, 2007, when
Kentex completed a so-called short-form merger with its wholly-owned subsidiary,
Northern Oil and Gas, Inc. (&#8220;NOG&#8221;), a Nevada corporation engaged in the
Company&#8217;s current business, in which NOG merged into Kentex and Kentex was the
surviving entity.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s common stock trades on the American
Stock Exchange under the symbol &#8220;NOG&#8221;.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company will continue to focus on projects in the oil and gas industry primarily
based in the Rocky Mountains and specifically the Williston Basin Bakken Shale
formation. The Company has begun to develop its substantial leasehold in the
Bakken play and will continue to do so as well as target additional
opportunities in emerging plays utilizing its first mover leasing
advantage.&#160;&#160;We participate on a heads up basis in the drilling of
wells on our leasehold.&#160;&#160;We own working interest in wells, and do not
lease land to operators.&#160;&#160;To this point we have participated only in
wells operated by others but have a substantial inventory of high working
interest locations that we will likely drill in 2009 and beyond.&#160;&#160;We
believe the advantage gained by participating as a non-operating partner in the
over 100 gross oil wells completed as of June 30, 2009 has given us valuable
data on completions and will help our operating partners control well costs and
enhance results as we continue to develop our higher working interest sections
in mid-2009.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company participates on a heads up basis proportionate to its working interest
in a declared drilling unit.&#160;&#160;Although to this point we have
participated with minority interests ranging from 1% to 42%, we expect to
participate in the drilling of incrementally higher working interest drilling
units, eventually operating our substantial inventory of high working interest
drilling units with a range of 40% to 100% ownership.&#160;&#160;We control
approximately 70,000 net acres in the growing Williston Basin Bakken and Three
Forks Play.&#160;&#160;This exposes us to approximately 110 net wells based on
640 acre spacing units.&#160;&#160;To be more specific, if we drill a well and
participate with a 25% working interest, this counts towards this total as a
quarter of one well.&#160;&#160;Down spacing in the field will potentially
expose us to significantly more wells as development continues on &#8220;held by
production&#8221; acreage. Further, the productivity of the Three Forks/Sanish and
secondary recovery expose us to substantially more potential
reserves.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Our land
acquisition and field operations, along with various other services, are
primarily outsourced through the use of consultants and drilling
partners.&#160;&#160;The Company will continue to retain independent contractors
to assist in operating and managing the prospects as well as to carry out the
principal and necessary functions incidental to the oil and gas
business.&#160;&#160;With the additional acquisition of oil and natural gas
properties, the Company intends to continue to use both in-house employees and
outside consultants to develop and exploit its leasehold interests.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">As an
independent oil and gas producer, the Company&#8217;s revenue, profitability and
future rate of growth are substantially dependent on prevailing prices of
natural gas and oil.&#160;&#160;Historically, the energy markets have been very
volatile and it is likely that oil and gas prices will continue to be subject to
wide fluctuations in the future.&#160;&#160;A substantial or extended decline in
natural gas and oil prices could have a material adverse effect on the Company&#8217;s
financial position, results of operations, cash flows and access to capital, and
on the quantities of natural gas and oil reserves that can be economically
produced.&#160;&#160;</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">NOTE
2&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;SIGNIFICANT
ACCOUNTING PRACTICES</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="FIS_UNIDENTIFIED_TABLE_3">The financial information included herein is
unaudited, except the balance sheet as of December 31, 2008, which has been
derived from our audited financial statements as of December 31,
2008.&#160;&#160;However, such information includes all adjustments (consisting
solely of normal recurring adjustments), which are in the opinion of management,
necessary for a fair presentation of financial position, results of operations
and cash flows for the</a></font></div><br>
    <div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
      <div id="FTR">
        <div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
</font></div>
      </div>
      <div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
        <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">8</font></div>
        <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
          <hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">
        </div>
      </div>
      <div id="HDR">
        <div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
</font></div>
      </div>
    </div><br>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">interim
periods.&#160;&#160;The results of operations for interim periods are not
necessarily indicative of the results to be expected for an entire
year.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Certain
information, accounting policies, and footnote disclosures normally included in
the financial statements prepared in accordance with accounting principles
generally accepted in the United States of America have been condensed or
omitted in this Form 10-Q pursuant to certain rules and regulations of the
Securities and Exchange Commission.&#160;&#160;The financial statements should
be read in conjunction with the audited financial statements for the year ended
December 31, 2008, which were included in our Annual Report on Form 10-K for the
fiscal year ended December 31, 2008.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="eolPage9"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Cash,
Cash Equivalents, and Long-Term Investments</font></a></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company considers highly liquid investments with insignificant interest rate
risk and original maturities to the Company of three months or less to be cash
equivalents.&#160;&#160;Cash equivalents consist primarily of interest-bearing
bank accounts and money market funds.&#160;&#160;Our cash positions represent
assets held in checking and money market accounts.&#160;&#160;These assets are
generally available to us on a daily or weekly basis and are highly liquid in
nature.&#160;&#160;Due to the balances being greater than $250,000, we do not
have FDIC coverage on the entire amount of bank deposits.&#160;&#160;The Company
believes this risk is minimal.&#160;&#160;In addition, we are subject to SIPC
protection on a vast majority of our financial assets.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Other Property and
Equipment</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Property
and equipment that are not oil and gas properties are recorded at cost and
depreciated using the straight-line method over their estimated useful lives of
three to five years.&#160;&#160;Expenditures for replacements, renewals, and
betterments are capitalized.&#160;&#160;Maintenance and repairs are charged to
operations as incurred.&#160;&#160;Long-lived assets, other than oil and gas
properties, are evaluated for impairment to determine if current circumstances
and market conditions indicate the carrying amount may not be
recoverable.&#160;&#160;We have not recognized any impairment losses on non oil
and gas long-lived assets.&#160;&#160;Depreciation expense was $45,456 for the
six months ended June 30, 2009.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Debt Issuance
Costs</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
February 2009, the Company entered into a revolving credit facility with CIT
Capital USA, Inc. (CIT) (see Note 9).&#160; The Company incurred costs related
to this facility that were capitalized on the Balance Sheet as Debt Issuance
Costs.&#160; Included in the Debt Issuance Costs are direct costs paid to third
parties for broker fees and legal fees, 180,000 shares of restricted common
stock paid as additional compensation for broker fees, and the fair value of
300,000 warrants issued to CIT.&#160; The fair value of the warrants was
calculated using the Black-Sholes valuation model based on factors present at
the time of closing.&#160; CIT can exercise these warrants at any time until the
warrants expire in February 2012.&#160; The exercise price of the warrants is
$5.00 per warrant.&#160; The total amount capitalized for Debt Issuance Costs is
$1,670,000.&#160; The capitalized costs will be amortized for three years over
the term of the facility using the effective interest
method.&#160;&#160;&#160;In May 2009, the Company amended the revolving credit
facility with CIT to allow for additional borrowings.&#160;&#160;The Company
incurred $216,414 of direct costs related to this</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">amendment.&#160;&#160;The
capitalized costs will be amortized over the remaining term of the facility
using the effective interest method.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
amortization of debt issuance costs for the six months ended June 30, 2009 was
$168,790.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Asset Retirement
Obligations</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company records the fair value of a liability for an asset retirement obligation
in the period in which the asset is acquired and a corresponding increase in the
carrying amount of the related long-lived asset.&#160;&#160;The liability is
accreted to its present value each period, and the capitalized cost is
depreciated over the useful life of the related asset.&#160;&#160;If the
liability is settled for an amount other than the recorded amount, a gain or
loss is recognized.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Revenue Recognition and Gas
Balancing</font></font></div><br>
    <div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
      <div id="FTR">
        <div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
</font></div>
      </div>
      <div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
        <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">9</font></div>
        <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
          <hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">
        </div>
      </div>
      <div id="HDR">
        <div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
</font></div>
      </div>
    </div><br>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">We
recognize oil and gas revenues from our interests in producing wells when
production is delivered to, and title has transferred to, the purchaser and to
the extent the selling price is reasonably determinable.&#160;&#160;We use the
sales method of accounting for gas balancing of gas production and would
recognize a liability if the existing proven reserves were not adequate to cover
the current imbalance situation.&#160;&#160;As of June 30, 2009 and December 31,
2008, our gas production was in balance, i.e., our cumulative portion of gas
production taken and sold from wells in which we have an interest equaled our
entitled interest in gas production from those wells.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Stock-Based
Compensation</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company has accounted for stock-based compensation under the provisions of
Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No. 123(R), &#8220;Share-Based
Payment.&#8221;&#160;&#160;This statement requires us to record an expense associated
with the fair value of stock-based compensation.&#160;&#160;We currently use the
Black-Scholes option valuation model to calculate stock based compensation at
the date of grant.&#160;&#160;Option pricing models require the input of highly
subjective assumptions, including the expected price
volatility.&#160;&#160;Changes in these assumptions can materially affect the
fair value estimate.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Income
Taxes</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company accounts for income taxes under FASB Statement No. 109, &#8220;Accounting for
Income Taxes.&#8221;&#160;&#160;Deferred income tax assets and liabilities are
determined based upon differences between the financial reporting and tax bases
of assets and liabilities and are measured using the enacted tax rates and laws
that will be in effect when the differences are expected to
reverse.&#160;&#160;SFAS 109 requires the consideration of a valuation allowance
for deferred tax assets if it is &#8220;more likely than not&#8221; that some component or
all of the benefits of deferred tax assets will not be realized.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt">&#160;</font><a name="eolPage10" /><a name="FORM10Q_05112009_HTM_EOLPAGE51"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Stock Issuance
</font></a></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company records the stock-based compensation awards issued to non-employees and
other external entities for goods and services at either the fair market value
of the goods received or services rendered or the instruments issued in exchange
for such services, whichever is more readily determinable, using the measurement
date guidelines enumerated in EITF No. 96-18, &#8220;Accounting for Equity Instruments
That Are Issued to Other Than Employees for Acquiring or in Conjunction with
Selling, Goods, or Services.&#8221;</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Net Income (Loss) Per Common
Share</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;&#160;</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Basic
earnings per share (EPS) is computed by dividing net income (the numerator) by
the weighted average number of common shares outstanding for the period (the
denominator).&#160;&#160;Diluted EPS is computed by dividing net income by the
weighted average number of common shares and potential common shares outstanding
(if dilutive) during each period.&#160;&#160;Potential common shares include
stock options, warrants, and restricted stock.&#160;&#160;The number of
potential common shares outstanding relating to stock options, warrants, and
restricted stock is computed using the treasury stock method.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
reconciliation of the denominators used to calculate basic EPS and diluted EPS
for the three and six months ended June 30, 2009 and 2008 are as follows (in
thousands):</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">As of

that became exercisable in 2007.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">&#160;</div>
    <div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
      <div id="FTR">
        <div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left">
        </div>
      </div>
      <div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
        <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">10</font></div>
        <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
          <hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">
        </div>
      </div>
      <div id="HDR">
        <div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right">
        </div>
      </div>
    </div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
addition, as of June 30, 2009, there were 300,000 warrants that were issued in
conjunction with the February 2009 revolving credit facility with CIT Capital
USA, Inc. that remained outstanding and exercisable.&#160; These warrants are
presently exercisable and represent potentially dilutive shares.&#160; Each of
these warrants has an exercise price of $5.00.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Full Cost
Method</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company follows the full cost method of accounting for oil and gas operations
whereby all costs related to the exploration and development of oil and gas
properties are initially capitalized into a single cost center (&#8220;full cost
pool&#8221;).&#160;&#160;Such costs include land acquisition costs, geological and
geophysical expenses, carrying charges on non-producing properties, costs of
drilling directly related to acquisition, and exploration
activities.&#160;&#160;Internal costs that are capitalized are directly
attributable to acquisition, exploration and development activities and do not
include costs related to the production, general corporate overhead or similar
activities.&#160;&#160;Costs associated with production and general corporate
activities are expensed in the period incurred.&#160;&#160;The Company
capitalized $406,165 of internal costs and $178,503 of interest for the six
months ended June 30, 2009.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">As of
June 30, 2009 we controlled acreage in Sheridan County, Montana with primary
targets including the Red River and Mission&#160;Canyon. We controlled acreage
in North Dakota, primarily in Mountrail&#160;County, targeting the Bakken Shale
and Three Forks/Sanish as well as acreage in Yates County, New York that is
prospective for Marcellus Shale and Trenton-Black&#160;River natural gas
production. Proceeds from property sales will generally be credited to the full
cost pool, with no gain or loss recognized, unless such a sale would
significantly alter the relationship between capitalized costs and the proved
reserves attributable to these costs.&#160;&#160;A significant alteration would
typically involve a sale of 25% or more of the proved reserves related to a
single full cost pool.&#160;&#160;In the year ended December 31, 2008 the
Company sold acreage for $468,609.&#160;&#160;The proceeds for these sales were
applied to reduce the capitalized costs of oil and gas properties. There were no
property sales for the six months ended June 30, 2009.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Capitalized
costs associated with impaired properties and capitalized cost related to
properties having proved reserves, plus the estimated future development costs,
asset retirement costs under Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No. 143
&#8220;Accounting for Asset Retirement Obligations&#8221; (SFAS 143) are depleted and
amortized on the unit-of-production method based on the estimated gross proved
reserves as determined by independent petroleum engineers.&#160;&#160;The costs
of unproved properties are withheld from the depletion base until such time as
they are either developed or abandoned.&#160;&#160;When proved reserves are
assigned or the property is considered to be impaired, the cost of the property
or the amount of the impairment is added to costs subject to depletion
calculations.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="eolPage11" /><a name="FORM10Q_05112009_HTM_EOLPAGE53">Capitalized costs of oil
and gas properties (net of related deferred income taxes) may not exceed an
amount equal to the present value, discounted at 10% per annum, of the estimated
future net cash flows from proved oil and gas reserves plus the cost of
unevaluated properties (adjusted for related income tax
effects).&#160;&#160;Should capitalized costs exceed this ceiling, impairment is
recognized.&#160;&#160;The present value of estimated future net cash flows is
computed by applying period-end prices of oil and natural gas to estimated
future production of proved oil and gas reserves as of period-end, less
estimated future expenditures to be incurred in developing and producing the
proved reserves and assuming continuation of existing economic
conditions.&#160;&#160;Such present value of proved reserves&#8217; future net cash
flows excludes future cash outflows associated with settling asset retirement
obligations that have been accrued on the Balance Sheet (following SEC Staff
Accounting Bulletin No. 106).&#160;&#160;Should this comparison indicate an
excess carrying value, the excess is charged to earnings as an impairment
expense.&#160;To this point the Company has not</a></font></div><br>
    <div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
      <div id="FTR">
        <div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
</font></div>
      </div>
      <div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
        <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">11</font></div>
        <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
          <hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">
        </div>
      </div>
      <div id="HDR">
        <div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
</font></div>
      </div>
    </div><br>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">realized
any impairment of its properties due to our low basis in the acreage and
productivity and economics of our producing wells.&#160; </font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Use of
Estimates</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
preparation of financial statements under generally accepted accounting
principles (&#8220;GAAP&#8221;) in the United States requires management to make estimates
and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and
disclosure of contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial
statements and the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the
reporting period.&#160;&#160;The most significant estimates relate to proved oil
and natural gas reserve volumes, future development costs, estimates relating to
certain oil and natural gas revenues and expenses, and deferred income
taxes.&#160;&#160;Actual results may differ from those estimates.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Derivative Instruments and
Price Risk Management</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company uses derivative instruments from time to time to manage market risks
resulting from fluctuations in the prices of oil and natural gas.&#160;&#160;The
Company may periodically enter into derivative contracts, including price swaps,
caps and floors, which require payments to (or receipts from) counterparties
based on the differential between a fixed price and a variable price for a fixed
quantity of oil or natural gas without the exchange of underlying
volumes.&#160;&#160;The notional amounts of these financial instruments would be
based on expected production from existing wells.&#160;&#160;The Company has,
and continues to use exchange traded futures contracts and option contracts to
hedge the delivery price of oil at a future date.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Derivatives
are recorded on the balance sheet at fair value and changes in the fair value of
derivatives are recorded each period in current earnings or other comprehensive
income, depending on whether a derivative is designated as part of a hedge
transaction and, if it is, depending on the type of hedge
transaction.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s derivatives consist primarily of cash flow
hedge transactions in which the Company is hedging the variability of cash flows
related to a forecasted&#160;transaction.&#160;&#160;Period to period changes in
the fair value of derivative instruments designated as cash flow hedges are
reported in other comprehensive income and reclassified to earnings in the
periods in which the contracts are settled.&#160;&#160;The ineffective portion
of the cash flow hedges is recognized in current period earnings as income or
loss from derivative.&#160;&#160;Gains and losses on derivative instruments that
do not qualify for hedge accounting are included in income or loss from
derivative in the period in which they occur.&#160;&#160;The resulting cash
flows from derivatives are reported as cash flows from operating
activities.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="FORM10Q_05112009_HTM_EOLPAGE54">At the inception of a derivative contract or
upon identification of hedged production to which a derivative contract applies,
the Company may designate the derivative as a cash flow hedge.&#160;&#160;For
all derivatives designated as cash flow hedges, the Company formally documents
the relationship between the derivative contract and the hedged items, as well
as the risk management objective for entering into the derivative
contract.&#160;&#160;To be designated as a cash flow hedge transaction, the
relationship between the derivative and the hedged items must be highly
effective in achieving the offset of changes in cash flows attributable to the
risk both at the inception of the derivative and on an ongoing
basis.&#160;&#160;The Company measures hedge effectiveness on a quarterly basis
and hedge accounting is discontinued prospectively if it is determined that the
derivative is no longer effective in offsetting changes in the cash flows of the
hedged item.&#160;&#160;Gains and losses deferred in accumulated other
comprehensive income related to cash flow hedge derivatives that become
ineffective remain unchanged until the related production is
delivered.&#160;&#160;If the Company determines that it is probable that a
hedged forecasted transaction will not occur, deferred gains or losses on the
</a><a name="FORM10Q_05112009_HTM_FORM10K_03162009_HT">derivative are recognized
in earnings immediately.&#160;&#160;See Note 14 for a description of the
derivative contracts which the Company executed during 2009.</a></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Impairment</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">SFAS 144,
&#8220;Accounting for the Impairment and Disposal of Long-Lived Assets,&#8221; requires that
long-lived assets to be held and used be reviewed for impairment whenever events
or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying amount of an asset may
not be recoverable.&#160;&#160;Oil and gas properties accounted for using the
full cost method of accounting (which we use) are excluded from this requirement
but continue to be subject to the full cost method&#8217;s impairment
rules.</font></div><br>
    <div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
      <div id="FTR">
        <div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
</font></div>

      <div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always">
        <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">12</font></div>

</font></div>
      </div>
    </div><br>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">New Accounting
Pronouncements</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="eolPage12">In March 2008, the FASB issued SFAS No. 161, "Disclosures about
Derivative Instruments and Hedging Activities."&#160;&#160;SFAS 161 is intended
to improve financial reporting about derivative instruments and hedging
activities by requiring enhanced disclosures to enable investors to better
understand their effects on an entity's financial position, financial
performance, and cash flows.&#160;&#160;SFAS 161 is effective for financial
statements issued for fiscal years and interim periods beginning after November
15, 2008, with early application encouraged.&#160;&#160;Pursuant to the
transition provisions of the Statement, the Company adopted SFAS No.&#160;161 on
January&#160;1, 2009.&#160;&#160;The required disclosures are presented in Note
14 on a prospective basis. This Statement does not impact the financial results
as it is disclosure-only in nature.</a></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
April&#160;2009, the FASB issued FSP FAS 107-1 and Accounting Principles Board
(APB) 28-1 &#8220;Interim Disclosures about Fair Value of Financial Instruments&#8221;. The
FSP amends SFAS No.&#160;107 &#8220;Disclosures about Fair Value of Financial
Instruments&#8221; to require an entity to provide disclosures about fair value of
financial instruments in interim financial information. This FSP is to be
applied prospectively and is effective for interim and annual periods ending
after June&#160;15, 2009 with early adoption permitted for periods ending after
March&#160;15, 2009. The required disclosures are presented in&#160;&#160;Note
12 of a prospective basis.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
February&#160;2008, the FASB issued FSP FAS 157-2, &#8220;Effective Date of FASB
Statement No.&#160;157.&#8221; FSP FAS 157-2 delayed the effective date of SFAS
No.&#160;157 &#8220;Fair Value Measurements&#8221; from 2008 to 2009 for all nonfinancial
assets and nonfinancial liabilities, except those that are recognized or
disclosed at fair value in the financial statements on a recurring basis (at
least annually). The adoption of the provisions of SFAS No.&#160;157 related to
nonfinancial assets and nonfinancial liabilities on January&#160;1, 2009 did not
have a material impact on the Financial Statements. See Note 12 for SFAS
No.&#160;157 disclosures.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In April
2009, the FASB issued Staff Position SFAS 157-4, &#8220;Determining Fair Value When
the Volume and Level of Activity for the Asset or Liability Have Significantly
Decreased and Identifying Transactions That Are Not Orderly&#8221; (FSP
157-4).&#160;&#160;FSP 157-4 provides additional guidance in estimating fair
value under statement No. 157, &#8220;Fair Value Measurements&#8221; (SFAS 157), when the
volume and level of transaction activity for an asset or liability have
significantly decreased in relation to normal market activity for the asset or
liability.&#160;&#160;FSP 157-4 also provides additional guidance on
circumstances that may indicate a transaction is not orderly.&#160;&#160;FSP
157-4 is effective for interim periods ending after June 15, 2009, and the
Company has adopted its provisions during second quarter 2009.&#160;&#160;FSP
157-4 did not have a significant impact on the Company&#8217;s financial position,
results of operations, cash flows, or disclosures for second quarter
2009.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt">&#160;</div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
April&#160;2009, the FASB issued FSP FAS 115-2 and FAS 124-2 &#8220;Recognition and
Presentation of Other-Than-Temporary Impairments&#8221;. The guidance applies to
investments in debt securities for which other-than-temporary impairments may be
recorded. If an entity&#8217;s management asserts that it does not have the intent to
sell a debt security and it is more likely than not that it will not have to
sell the security before recovery of its cost basis, then an entity may separate
other-than-temporary impairments into two components: 1) the amount related to
credit losses (recorded in earnings), and 2) all other amounts (recorded in
other comprehensive income). This FSP is to be applied prospectively and is
effective for interim and annual periods ending after June&#160;15, 2009 with
early adoption permitted for periods ending after March&#160;15, 2009. The
adoption of the provisions of this FSP in the second quarter 2009 did not have a
material impact on the Financial Statements.</font></div><br>
    <div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
      <div id="FTR">
        <div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;

        <div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">13</font></div>

          <hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">
        </div>

      <div id="HDR">
        <div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
</font></div>
      </div>
    </div><br>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In June
2009, the FASB issued SFAS No. 166, &#8220;Accounting for Transfers of Financial
Assets&#8221; (SFAS No. 166). SFAS No. 166 amends the derecognition guidance in SFAS
No. 140, Accounting for Transfers and Servicing of Financial Assets and
Extinguishments of Liabilities (SFAS No. 140). SFAS No. 166 is effective for
fiscal years beginning after November 15, 2009. The Company is currently
assessing the impact of SFAS No. 166 on its financial position and results of
operations.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In June
2009, the FASB issued Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No. 167,
Amendments to FASB Interpretation No. 46(R) (&#8220;FAS 167&#8221;). FAS 167 amends FASB
Interpretation No. 46(R), Consolidation of Variable Interest Entities, (&#8220;FIN 46
(R)&#8221;) to eliminate the quantitative approach previously required for determining
the primary beneficiary of a variable interest entity and requires a qualitative
analysis to determine whether an enterprise&#8217;s variable interest gives it a
controlling financial interest in a variable interest entity. FAS 167 amends
certain guidance in FIN 46(R) for determining whether an entity is a variable
interest entity. This statement also requires ongoing reassessments of whether
an enterprise is the primary beneficiary of a variable interest entity. FAS 167
will be effective as of the beginning of the Company&#8217;s 2010 fiscal year. The
Company is currently evaluating the impact of the adoption of
FAS&#160;167.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In June
2009, the FASB issued Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No. 168, The
FASB Accounting Standards Codification<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 70%; VERTICAL-ALIGN: super">&#8482;</font> and the
Hierarchy of Generally Accepted Accounting Principles, a replacement of FASB
Statement No. 162 (&#8220;FAS 168&#8221;). Under FAS 168, the FASB Accounting Standards
Codification<font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 70%; VERTICAL-ALIGN: super">&#8482;</font> (the
&#8220;Codification&#8221;) will become the exclusive source of authoritative U.S. generally
accepted accounting principles (&#8220;U.S. GAAP&#8221;) recognized by the FASB to be
applied by nongovernmental entities. Rules and interpretive releases of the
Securities and Exchange Commission (&#8220;SEC&#8221;) under authority of federal securities
laws are also sources of authoritative GAAP for SEC registrants. The
Codification will supersede all then-existing non-SEC accounting and reporting
standards, with the exception of certain non-SEC accounting literature which
will become nonauthoritative. FAS 168 is effective for the Company&#8217;s 2009 third
fiscal quarter. The adoption of FAS 168 will not have a material impact on the
Company&#8217;s Financial Statements. All references to U.S. GAAP provided in the
notes to the Financial Statements will be updated to conform to the
Codification.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In May
2009, the FASB issued SFAS No. 165, &#8220;Subsequent Events&#8221; (SFAS No. 165). SFAS No.
165 provides guidance on management&#8217;s assessment of subsequent events and
incorporates this guidance into accounting literature. SFAS No. 165 is effective
prospectively for interim and annual periods ending after June 15, 2009. The
implementation of this standard did not have a material impact on the Company&#8217;s
financial position and results of operations. The Company has evaluated
subsequent events through July 30, 2009, the date of issuance of the Company&#8217;s
financial position and results of operations.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">NOTE
3&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;SHORT-TERM
INVESTMENTS</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">All
marketable debt and equity securities that are included in short-term
investments are considered available-for-sale and are carried at fair
value.&#160;&#160;The unrealized gains and losses related to these securities
are included in accumulated other comprehensive income (loss).&#160;&#160; When
securities are sold, their cost is determined based on the first-in first-out
method.&#160;&#160;The realized gains and losses related to these securities are
included in other income in the statements of
operations.&#160;&#160;</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">For the
six months ended June 30, 2009 there were no realized gains or losses recognized
on the sale of investments.&#160;&#160;In November 2008 we received, in a
settlement from UBS AG (&#8220;UBS&#8221;), rights which allow us to put back the auction
rate securities at par value to UBS.&#160;&#160;We expect to liquidate these
investments at par no later than June 2010, in the meantime they continue to pay
interest at various rates.&#160;&#160;We also have the ability to borrow up to
75% of the loan-to-market value of eligible <a name="eolPage13">auction rate
securities on a no-net cost basis.&#160;&#160;As of June 30, 2009, we have
borrowed $1,638,382 under the agreement, with an additional $480,368 of
borrowings available under the agreement.&#160;</a></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company reviews these investments on a quarterly basis to determine if it is
probable that the Company will realize some portion of the unrealized loss in
accordance with SFAS&#160;No.&#160;115, and FSP No. FAS 115-1 and
FAS&#160;124-1, &#8220;The Meaning of Other-Than-Temporary Impairment and Its
Application to Certain Investments,&#8221; and to determine the classification of the
impairment as temporary or other-than-temporary.&#160;&#160;&#160;In determining
if the difference between cost and estimated fair value of the auction rate
securities was deemed either temporary or other-than-temporary impairment, the
Company evaluated each type of short-term investment using a set of criteria
including decline in value, duration of the decline, period until anticipated
recovery, nature of investment, probability of recovery, financial condition and
near-term prospects of the issuer, the Company&#8217;s intent and ability to retain
the investment, attributes of the decline in value, status with rating agencies,
status of principal and interest payments and any other issues related to the
underlying securities. The Company determined the decline in the fair values in
all of the investments in the auction rate securities were temporary as of June
30, 2009, primarily based on estimated cash flows of the investments, the
settlement agreement entered into with UBS, and the Company&#8217;s ability and intent
to hold such investments until settlement.</font></div>

      <div id="HDR">
        <div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
</font></div>
      </div>
    </div><br>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">NOTE
5&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;OIL
AND GAS PROPERTIES</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Acquisition</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In May
2009, the Company entered into an exploration and development agreement with
Slawson Exploration Company, Inc. (Slawson) pursuant to which the Company
acquired certain North Dakota Bakken assets from Windsor Bakken LLC as part of a
syndicate led by privately owned Slawson.&#160; Pursuant to the agreement, the
Company purchased a five percent (5.0%) interest of the undeveloped acreage,
including approximately 60,000 net acres.&#160; The Company also acquired an
additional nine percent (9%) interest in the existing well bores purchased from
Windsor Bakken LLC, providing the Company an aggregate fourteen percent (14%)
interest in the existing 59 gross Bakken and Three Forks well bores in North
Dakota including approximately 1,200 barrels of oil production per day.&#160; In
the transaction, the Company purchased approximately 300,000 barrels of proven
producing reserves as well as approximately 3,000 net undeveloped
acres.&#160;&#160;The Company paid a total cost of $7,300,000 for the initial
acquisition of acreage and well bore interests.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">NOTE
6&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;PREFERRED
AND COMMON STOCK</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company has neither authorized nor issued any shares of preferred
stock.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">On April
3, 2009 the Company acquired leasehold interests in North Dakota. The total
consideration paid for this acreage was 49,092 shares of restricted common
stock.&#160; The fair value of the restricted stock was $224,879. The restricted
common stock related to this acquisition will be issued as soon as
possible.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">On
February 27, 2009, the Company closed on a revolving credit facility with CIT
Capital USA, Inc. (CIT).&#160;&#160;As part of this credit facility agreement
the Company entered into an engagement with Cynergy Advisors, LLC
(Cynergy).&#160;&#160;As part of the compensation for the work performed on
obtaining the financing, Cynergy received 180,000 shares of restricted Common
Stock of the Company.&#160;&#160;The fair value of the restricted stock was
$475,200 or $2.64 per share, the market value of a share of Common Stock on the
date the financing closed.&#160;&#160;The fair value of this stock was
capitalized as Debt Issuance Costs and is being amortized for three years over
the term of the financing.&#160;&#160;</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In June
2009, the Company completed a registered direct offering of 2,250,000 shares of
common stock at a price of $6.00 per share for total gross proceeds of
$13,500,000.&#160; C.K. Cooper &amp; Company acted as lead placement agent on
the transaction for which it received consideration in cash.&#160;&#160;The
Company incurred costs of $798,951 related to this offering.&#160;&#160;These
costs were netted against the proceeds of the offering through Additional
Paid-In Capital.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">Restricted Stock
Awards</font></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In March
2008, the Company issued 20,000 shares of restricted common stock to employee
James Sankovitz pursuant to a written employment agreement.&#160;&#160;The
issuance of restricted stock is intended to retain and motivate the
employee.&#160;&#160;The fair value of the award was $140,500 or $7.03 per
share, the average market value of a share of Common Stock on the date the stock
was issued. The fair value was expensed over the one-year term of the
award.&#160;&#160;The Company expensed $35,125 related to this award in the six
months ended June 30, 2009.&#160;&#160;The shares are fully vested at June 30,
2009.&#160;&#160;Vesting of the shares was contingent on the employee
maintaining employment with the Company and other restrictions included in the
employment agreement.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
February 2009, the Company granted 60,000 shares of restricted common stock to
employees James Sankovitz and Chad Winter pursuant to written
agreements.&#160;&#160;The grants of restricted stock are intended to retain and
motivate the employees.&#160;&#160;The fair value of the awards was $170,400 or
$2.84 per share, the market value of a share of common stock on the date the
stock was granted.&#160;&#160;30,000 of the shares become fully vested on
January 1, 2010 and 30,000 of the shares become fully vested on January 1,
2011.&#160;&#160;The fair value will be expensed evenly over the term of the
award.&#160;&#160;The Company expensed $51,062 related to those awards in the
six months ended June 30, 2009.&#160;&#160;Vesting of the awards is contingent
on the employees maintaining employment with the Company and other restrictions
in the agreement.</font></div><br>

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In

three employees of the company.&#160;&#160;The employees are fully vested in the

amount of this stock award was expensed in the six months ended June 30,

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left">&#160;</div>

      <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In June
2009, the Company agreed to issue 18,000 shares of Common Stock to an employee

of common stock on the date the stock was obligated to be
issued.&#160;&#160;</font></div>

7&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;RELATED

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company has purchased leasehold interests from South Fork Exploration, LLC
(SFE).&#160;In the second quarter of 2009, the company paid a total of $53,603

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">NOTE
8&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;STOCK
OPTIONS/STOCK BASED COMPENSATION</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">On
November 1, 2007 the Board of Directors granted 560,000 of options under the
2006 Stock Option Plan.&#160;&#160;The Company granted 500,000 options, in
aggregate, to members of the board and 60,000 options to one employee pursuant
to an employment agreement.&#160;&#160;These options were granted at a price of
$5.18 per share and the optionees were fully vested on the grant
date.&#160;&#160;160,000 options granted in 2007 have been exercised as of June
30, 2009.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company accounts for stock-based compensation under the provisions of SFAS No.
123(R), &#8220;Share Based Payment.&#8221;&#160;&#160;This statement requires us to record
an expense associated with the fair value of stock-based
compensation.&#160;&#160;We currently use the Black-Scholes option valuation
model to calculate stock-based compensation at the date of
grant.&#160;&#160;Option pricing models require the input of highly subjective
assumptions, including the expected price volatility.&#160;&#160;Changes in
these assumptions can materially affect the fair value estimate.&#160;&#160;The
total fair value of the options will be recognized as compensation over the
vesting period.&#160;&#160;The Company received no cash consideration for these
option grants.&#160;&#160;There have been no stock options granted in 2008 or
2009 under the 2006 Stock Option Plan, and all exercises of options during 2008
related to prior period grants.</font></div>

      <div id="HDR">
        <div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
</font></div>
      </div>
    </div><br>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><a name="eolPage15">NOTE 9&#160;&#160;REVOLVING CREDIT FACILITY</a></font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In
February 2009, the Company completed the closing of a revolving credit facility
with CIT Capital USA Inc. (&#8220;CIT&#8221;) that will provide up to a maximum principal
amount of $25 million of working capital for exploration and production
operations (the &#8220;Facility&#8221;).&#160;&#160;The borrowing base of funds available
under the Facility will be redetermined semi-annually based upon the net present
value, discounted at 10% per annum, of the future net revenues expected to
accrue from its interests in proved reserves estimated to be produced from its
oil and gas properties.&#160;&#160;$11 million of financing was initially
available under the Facility.&#160;&#160;In May 2009 CIT agreed to increase the
current amount available under the Facility to $16 million in conjunction with
the acquisition of certain assets of Windsor Bakken, LLC (see Note
5).&#160;&#160;An additional $9 million of financing could become available upon
subsequent borrowing base redeterminations.&#160;&#160;The Facility terminates
on February 27, 2012, with all outstanding borrowings due at that
time.&#160;&#160;&#160;The Company had borrowed $16 million under the facility
at June 30, 2009.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company has the option to designate the reference rate of interest for each
specific borrowing under the Facility as amounts are
advanced.&#160;&#160;Borrowings based upon the London interbank offering rate
(LIBOR) will be outstanding for a period of one, three or six months (as
designated by us) and bear interest at a rate equal to 5.50% over the one-month,
three-month or six-month LIBOR rate to be no less than 2.50%.&#160;&#160;Any
borrowings not designated as being based upon LIBOR will have no specified term
and generally will bear interest at a rate equal to 4.50% over the greater of
(a) the current three-month LIBOR rate plus 1.0% or (b) the current prime rate
as published by JP Morgan Chase Bank, N.A.&#160;&#160;The Company has the option
to designate either pricing mechanism.&#160;&#160;Payments are due under the
Facility in arrears, in the case of a loan based on LIBOR on the last day of the
specified loan period and in the case of all other loans on the last day of each
March, June, September and December.&#160;&#160;All outstanding principal is due
and payable upon termination of the Facility. At June 30, 2009 the weighted
average interest rate on the outstanding borrowings was approximately
8.0%.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
applicable interest rate increases under the Facility and the lenders may
accelerate payments under the Facility, or call all obligations due under
certain circumstances, upon an event of default.&#160;&#160;The Facility
references various events constituting a default on the Facility, including, but
not limited to, failure to pay interest on any loan under the Facility, any
material violation of any representation or warranty under the Credit Agreement
in connection with the Facility, failure to observe or perform certain
covenants, conditions or agreements under the Facility, a change in control of
the Company, default under any other material indebtedness the Company might
have, bankruptcy and similar proceedings and failure to pay disbursements from
lines of credit issued under the Facility.&#160;&#160;The Company was not in
default on the Facility as of June 30, 2009, and is not expected to be in
default in the future.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Facility required that the Company enter into swap agreements with Macquarie
Bank Limited (&#8220;Macquarie&#8221;) for each month of the thirty-six (36) month period
following the date on which each such swap agreement is executed, the notional
volumes for which (when aggregated with other commodity swap agreements and
additional fixed-price physical off-take contracts then in effect other than
basis differential swaps on volumes already hedged pursuant to other swap
agreements), as of the date such swap agreement is executed, is not less than
50% of, nor exceeds 80% of, the reasonably anticipated projected production from
the Company&#8217;s proved developed producing reserves.&#160;&#160;The hedged
production is estimated to be equal to approximately 20% of 2009 total
production and less than 10% of production volumes in 2010-12.&#160;&#160;See
Note 14 for additional disclosure concerning these swap agreements.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">All of
the Company&#8217;s obligations under the Facility and the swap agreements with
Macquarie are secured by a first priority security interest in any and all
assets of the Company pursuant to the terms of a Guaranty and Collateral
Agreement and perfected by a mortgage, notice of pledge and security and similar
documents.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">NOTE
10&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;ASSET
RETIREMENT OBLIGATION</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company has asset retirement obligations associated with the future plugging and
abandonment of proved properties and related facilities.&#160;&#160;Under the
provisions of SFAS 143, the fair value of a liability for an asset retirement
obligation is recorded in the period in which it is incurred and a corresponding
increase in the carrying amount of the related long lived asset.&#160;&#160;The
liability is accreted to its present value each period, and the
capitalized</font></div><br>
    <div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
      <div id="FTR">
        <div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; COLOR: #000000; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;
</font></div>
      </div>

          <hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">

</font></div>
      </div>
    </div><br>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">cost is
depreciated over the useful life of the related asset.&#160;&#160;If the
liability is settled for an amount other than the recorded amount, a gain or
loss is recognized.&#160;&#160;The Company has no assets that are legally
restricted for purposes of settling asset retirement
obligations.&#160;&#160;</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">NOTE
11&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;INCOME
TAXES</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The
Company utilizes the asset and liability approach to measuring deferred tax
assets and liabilities based on temporary differences existing at each balance
sheet date using currently enacted tax rates in accordance with SFAS
No.&#160;109, &#8220;Accounting for Income Taxes&#8221;.&#160;&#160;Deferred tax assets are
reduced by a valuation allowance when, in the opinion of management, it is more
likely than not that some portion or all of the deferred tax assets will not be
realized. Deferred tax assets and liabilities are adjusted for the effects of
changes in tax laws and rates on the date of enactment.</font></div>

income tax expense (benefit) for the six months ended June 30, 2009 and 2008

    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">In June
2006, the FASB issued Interpretation No. 48 &#8220;Accounting for Uncertainty in
Income Taxes, and Interpretation of FASB Statement No. 109&#8221; (FIN
48).&#160;&#160;We adopted FIN 48 on January 1, 2007.&#160;&#160;Under FIN 48,
tax benefits are recognized only for tax positions that are more likely than not
to be sustained upon examination by tax authorities.&#160;&#160;The amount
recognized is measured as the largest amount of benefit that is greater than 50
percent likely to be realized upon ultimate settlement.&#160;&#160;Unrecognized
tax benefits are tax benefits claimed in our tax returns that do not meet these
recognition and measurement standards.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Upon the
adoption of FIN 48, we had no liabilities for unrecognized tax benefits and, as
such, the adoption had no impact on our financial statements, and we have
recorded no additional interest or penalties.&#160;&#160;The adoption of FIN 48
did not impact our effective tax rates.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Our
policy is to recognize potential interest and penalties accrued related to
unrecognized tax benefits within income tax expense.&#160;&#160;For the six
months ended June 30, 2009, we did not recognize any interest or penalties in
our Statement of Operations, nor did we have any interest or penalties accrued
in our Balance Sheet at June 30, 2009 relating to unrecognized
benefits.</font></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br></div>
    <div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The tax
years 2008, 2007 and 2006 remain open to examination for federal income tax
purposes and by the other major taxing jurisdictions to which we are
subject.</font></div><br>
